19:622:51295:26:18:79:525:266:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:We focus on three related measures of French treatment; these are summarized in Table 1 for all
19:623:51390:18:19:79:525:248:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:states in our datasets. The first records for each country the years of French occupation between
19:624:51487:19:18:79:525:229:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the entire period 1792 and 1815.  We consider years in which the French had direct control
19:625:51577:18:18:79:525:211:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:over  these  territories  or  installed  republics  and  principalities  directly  dependent  on  French
19:626:51681:18:19:79:525:193:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:directives; we exclude years and months of pure military occupation, such as for example in
19:627:51772:19:18:79:171:174:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the case of Prussia.
19:628:51792:18:16:96:525:156:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Our  second  measure  is  binary  and  reports  as  treated  the  areas  invaded  by  the  French
19:629:51889:16:15:87:525:140:6:g_d0_f4:9:g_d0_f5:22The complete city level population dataset has information on all 2,200 European cities which had, at some
19:630:51997:15:11:79:525:125:9:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f5:time between 800 and 1800, 5,000 or more inhabitants.  City level populations are added up and divided by total
19:631:52108:11:11:79:525:114:9:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f5:population, as garnered from McEvedy and Jones (1978), Lahmeyer (n.d.)  or Maddison (2003).  The Bairoch et
19:632:52215:11:11:79:525:103:9:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f5:al.  dataset stops in 1850; therefore, we resort to official statistics of that period to estimate urbanization rates
19:633:52332:11:0:79:486:92:9:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f5:after that date.  More details on the construction of urbanization figures are provided in Appendix 6.
20:634:52436:0:18:79:525:671:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:revolutionary armies, thus the Netherlands, Belgium, Switzerland, most of northern and central
20:635:52530:18:19:79:525:653:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Italy as well as the Rhineland.  The third measure includes countries occupied by Napoleon.
20:636:52621:19:18:79:525:634:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:This adds Spain, Poland, most of Italy and the northwest of Germany.  The untreated countries
20:637:52714:18:19:79:525:616:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:are all those in Europe which were not occupied and for which we have data.  This includes
20:638:52804:19:18:79:525:597:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Britain, Portugal, Austria, Scandinavia, Eastern Europe, and the southern and eastern German
20:639:52896:18:19:79:525:579:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:states Baden, W ̈urttemberg, Bavaria, Saxony, and Prussia.  To the extent that some of these
20:640:52988:19:18:79:525:560:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:implemented modernizing reforms under pressure from France, through the implicit or explicit
20:641:53080:18:29:79:525:542:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:threat of invasion, this coding works against our hypothesis and biases our results downwards.
20:642:53174:29:26:79:357:513:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:3.3    Coding Institutional Reforms in Germany
20:643:53220:26:18:79:525:487:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:In the last part of our analysis, we also use an index of reforms in Germany, both to show the
20:644:53314:18:19:79:525:469:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:impact of the French occupation on institutional reforms and as the right-hand side variable
20:645:53406:19:18:79:525:450:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:in  our  instrumental-variables  strategy.   For  our  8  polities  in  Germany  we  were  also  able  to
20:646:53511:18:18:79:525:432:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:use historical sources to code the nature of some of the reforms that took place.  The reforms
20:647:53605:18:19:79:525:414:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:we  focus  on  are  the  enactment  of  written  legal  codes  including  the  French  civil  code,  the
20:648:53709:19:18:79:525:395:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:restructuring of agricultural relations, the abolition of guilds, and the emancipation of Jews.
20:649:53804:18:19:79:525:377:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:We  interpret  these  reforms  as  a  proxy  or  index  for  the  overall  set  of  institutional  reforms,
20:650:53911:19:18:79:525:358:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:which  also  include  changes  in  the  nature  of  state  administration  or  tax  collection  and  the
20:651:54015:18:19:79:525:340:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:secularization of church lands.  We are not able to construct measures of these reforms that are
20:652:54111:19:18:79:525:321:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:comparable across different areas of Germany (for example, the secularization of church lands
20:653:54204:18:18:79:525:303:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:was only relevant for Catholic territories).  Table 2 shows the incidence of reforms in Germany.
20:654:54300:18:19:96:525:285:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Looking first at the top panel of Table 2, the first three columns report the treatment status
20:655:54394:19:18:79:525:266:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:for the 8 German polities for each of the three definitions of treatment.  Column 1, for example,
20:656:54491:18:19:79:525:248:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:shows that only what was to become the Prussian Rhine Province (the Rhineland) was treated
20:657:54581:19:18:79:525:229:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:during the Revolutionary period.  In column 2, the Napoleonic treatment also includes Hanover
20:658:54674:18:18:79:525:211:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:and Westphalia (the latter also became part of Prussia after 1815).  In column 3 we record
20:659:54764:18:19:79:525:193:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the years of French control,  which ranges for 19 years for the Rhineland to just 3 years for
20:660:54857:19:18:79:121:174:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Hanover.
20:661:54865:18:19:96:525:156:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:The next four columns record the date at which the different polities introduced the various
20:662:54957:19:18:79:525:137:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:reforms on which we focus.  Appendix 6 describes in detail how we coded these reform dates
20:663:55047:18:19:79:525:119:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:and the sources we used.  The first is the date at which a written legal code was introduced.
20:664:55140:19:0:79:525:100:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:The figures in this column indicate both the presence of a written civil code, and of a system
21:665:55236:0:18:79:525:671:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:of  commercial  law,  represented  either  by  the  French  code  de  commerce,  or  by  the  Prussian
21:666:55338:18:19:79:525:653:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f2:Allgemeines Landrecht(ALR).23The Napoleonic civil code was introduced in 1805 in French-
21:667:55426:19:18:79:525:634:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:occupied Rhineland and in 1808 in Westphalia.  Other places such as Bavaria did not have such
21:668:55519:18:19:79:525:616:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:a code until 1900.  Note that although Baden was never treated it introduced a version of the
21:669:55612:19:18:79:525:597:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:French civil code in 1810.  The next column examines agrarian reform, effectively abolition of
21:670:55706:18:19:79:525:579:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:serfdom or alternative feudal landholding arrangements, such as theGrundherrschaft, prevalent
21:671:55799:19:18:79:525:560:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:in south and west Germany (though in many cases peasants had to pay a compensation to
21:672:55884:18:18:79:525:542:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:their landlords).  These reforms seem to have been relatively ineffective during the Napoleonic
21:673:55979:18:19:79:525:524:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:period itself even in the treated areas with the exception of the Rhineland.  Column 6 of the
21:674:56072:19:18:79:525:505:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:table records when guilds were abolished.  As this column reports, the abolition of guilds was
21:675:56166:18:19:79:525:487:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:one  of  the  reforms  most  assiduously  implemented  by  the  French,  but  something  that  only
21:676:56265:19:18:79:525:468:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:happened elsewhere in Germany some 50 years later.  Finally, column 7 presents data on the
21:677:56355:18:19:79:525:450:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:emancipation  of  the  Jews.   Though  some  historians  have  argued  for  the  importance  of  this
21:678:56456:19:18:79:525:431:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:(Ferguson, 1998), the evidence does not suggest that these reforms were actually enacted very
21:679:56549:18:18:79:525:413:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:effectively.  In most German states, full formal emancipation had to wait until the second half
21:680:56644:18:19:79:267:395:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:of the 19th century to be implemented.
21:681:56682:19:18:96:525:376:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:In  column  8  we  construct  a  simple  index  of  reforms  at  two  exemplary  dates,  1850  and
21:682:56780:18:19:79:525:358:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:1900 for each polity by simply adding the number of years each particular reform had been
21:683:56869:19:18:79:525:339:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:in place and dividing by 4.  As an example, consider Hanover, which was taken over by the
21:684:56958:18:19:79:525:321:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:French for such a brief period that reforms were not implemented.  By 1850 there had yet to
21:685:57049:19:18:79:525:302:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:be a written civil code; agrarian reform had been in place for 19 years; guilds had not been
21:686:57141:18:18:79:525:284:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:abolished; and Jews had not been emancipated.  Therefore the value of the index for Hanover
21:687:57232:18:19:79:525:266:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:in 1850 is 19/4=4.75.  This index shows a clear distinction between parts of western Germany
21:688:57324:19:18:79:525:247:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:that were reformed by the French, those places which defensively modernized, like Prussia or
21:689:57416:18:19:79:525:229:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Baden,  and  the  rest  of  Germany.   In  1850,  for  instance,  the  reform  index  was  33.5  for  the
21:690:57521:19:18:79:525:210:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Rhineland  and  27.25  for  Westphalia.   The  fact  that  it  was  31.25  for  Prussia  and  26.25  for
21:691:57625:18:19:79:525:192:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Baden shows how important the IV strategy is to avoid our results being biased by defensive
21:692:57716:19:18:79:525:173:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:modernization.   Figure  1  plots  the  reform  index  over  time  showing  the  divergence  between
21:693:57816:18:18:79:525:155:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:treated  areas  (Rhineland,  Westphalia),  defensive  modernization  areas  (Prussia,  Baden)  and
21:694:57914:18:19:79:177:137:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the rest of Germany.
21:695:57934:19:16:96:525:118:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:The  bottom  panel  of  Table  2  reports  some  of  the  data  in  an  intuitive  form.   We  show
21:696:58033:16:15:87:525:102:6:g_d0_f4:9:g_d0_f5:23The French implemented the civil code and the commercial code simultaneously and the ALR includes both
21:697:58137:15:0:79:453:87:9:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f5:types of codes, so we emphasized the timing of the introduction of both types of legal codes.
22:698:58232:0:18:79:525:671:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the average date that different reforms were implemented, by treatment status.  For instance,
22:699:58325:18:19:79:525:653:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:looking at the average date when guilds were abolished for polities which got the Napoleonic
22:700:58417:19:18:79:525:634:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:treatment, we see from column 6 that this was 1826, compared to 1853 for the control group.
22:701:58508:18:19:79:525:616:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:The last row of the table reports the correlation coefficient between the years of French control
22:702:58605:19:18:79:525:597:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:and the date when particular reforms were implemented.  For example, in column 4 we see that
22:703:58697:18:19:79:525:579:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the correlation between the date of introduction of a written civil code and years of French
22:704:58789:19:18:79:525:560:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:presence is -0.398,  so there is a sizable negative correlation—more years of French presence
22:705:58882:18:18:79:525:542:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:is correlated with an earlier introduction of a civil code.  As will be clear from the table, the
22:706:58979:18:29:79:382:524:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:correlation with respect to the abolition of guilds is the largest.
22:707:59046:29:25:79:177:495:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:3.4    Other Data
22:708:59063:25:19:79:525:470:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:We also use a variety of other data as controls, in particular the proportion of the population
22:709:59158:19:18:79:525:451:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:of a polity who are Protestant, the latitude of the capital city of the polity, and initial values
22:710:59256:18:28:79:203:433:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:of the dependent variable.
22:711:59282:28:26:79:234:405:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:3.5    Descriptive Statistics
22:712:59311:26:18:79:525:379:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Table 3A records some basic descriptive statistics of the complete cross-national dataset with
22:713:59405:18:19:79:525:361:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the standard deviations in parentheses below the means.  Panel A focuses on the urbanization
22:714:59497:19:18:79:475:342:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:dataset, while panel B examines the countries in the dataset with GDP per-capita.
22:715:59578:18:19:96:525:324:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:The table consists of five columns.  The first five rows describe urbanization rates in the
22:716:59669:19:18:79:525:305:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:five time periods considered;  this evolution is also depicted in Figures 2A and 2B. One sees
22:717:59762:18:18:79:525:287:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:that the urbanization rate prior to the revolutionary period was larger in polities that were
22:718:59855:18:19:79:525:269:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:invaded by the Revolutionary armies compared to those that were not.  The same is true with
22:719:59946:19:18:79:525:250:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:respect to the Napoleonic treatment.  This suggests that invaded countries were richer in 1700
22:720:60040:18:19:79:525:232:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:and also 1800.  Nevertheless, until 1800-1850 the urbanization rates of the two groups do not
22:721:60133:19:18:79:525:213:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:display different evolutions (if anything, there is a slight convergence of the untreated group
22:722:60228:18:19:79:525:195:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:toward the treated group).  So there seems to be little evidence of differential trends before the
22:723:60326:19:18:79:525:176:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:French Revolution.  After 1850, there is a marked take-off of the treated states relative to the
22:724:60422:18:18:79:100:158:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:rest.
22:725:60427:18:19:96:525:140:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:The next three rows of the table report summary statistics for the treatments status vari-
22:726:60517:19:18:79:525:121:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:ables.  Countries not invaded by French Revolutionary Armies still have 2.03 years of French
22:727:60609:18:19:79:525:103:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:presence on average (column 3), since they were later under Napoleonic control.  The next row
22:728:60702:19:0:79:525:84:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:shows average latitude, which does not vary significantly between the treatment and control
23:729:60795:0:18:79:525:671:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:groups.  The final row of this panel records the averages of our ‘Protestant’ variable,  which
23:730:60889:18:19:79:427:653:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:shows that untreated polities are in general more likely to be Protestant.
23:731:60963:19:18:96:525:634:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Panel B of Table 3A shows some similar patterns.  The sample is smaller now (since we
23:732:61048:18:19:79:525:616:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:do not have income variations within Germany or Italy) but we see that in 1700 income per-
23:733:61138:19:18:79:525:597:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:capita was higher in treated than in untreated areas and remained so throughout the period of
23:734:61231:18:19:79:522:579:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:analysis.  The picture with respect to latitude and Protestantism is also qualitatively similar.
23:735:61327:19:18:96:525:560:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:In Table 3B we turn to descriptive statistics for the 8 German polities.  In contrast to the
23:736:61419:18:18:79:525:542:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:whole sample we can see that, at least for the Napoleonic treatment,24there is little difference
23:737:61515:18:19:79:525:524:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:between the urbanization levels of treatment and control groups prior to 1789.  This is also
23:738:61607:19:18:79:525:505:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:shown in Figures 3A and 3B. Indeed,  in 1750 urbanization is slightly greater in the control
23:739:61699:18:19:79:525:487:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:group.  Subsequently, however, urbanization grows more rapidly in the treatment group so that
23:740:61792:19:34:79:454:468:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:by 1900 it is a full 10 percentage points higher in areas occupied by Napoleon.
23:741:61871:34:29:79:356:434:14:g_d0_f1:14:g_d0_f1:4    Cross-Country Regression Evidence
23:742:61909:29:19:79:525:405:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:In this section we use ordinary least squares (OLS) regressions to investigate the cross-country
23:743:62005:19:18:79:525:386:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:reduced-form relationship between our three measures of treatment and the two basic outcome
23:744:62096:18:19:79:525:368:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:variables, urbanization rates and log GDP per capita.  In all cases we have a panel dataset.
23:745:62188:19:18:79:525:349:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:For GDP per capita, the time periods are unevenly spread (e.g., from Maddison, 2003, we have
23:746:62280:18:18:79:525:331:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:income per capita for 1600, 1700, 1820, 1850, 1870, 1890 and 1900).  For urbanization we have
23:747:62373:18:19:79:342:313:11:g_d0_f2:8:g_d0_f3:data for the periods 1700, 1750, 1800, 1850 and 1900.25
23:748:62428:19:29:96:355:294:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Our basic reduced-form regression model is as follows:
23:749:62482:29:0:147:216:265:11:g_d0_f8:11:g_d0_f2:yjt=dt+δj+
23:750:62492:0:23:225:241:275:11:g_d0_f10:11:g_d0_f10:∑
23:751:62493:23:0:219:245:252:8:g_d0_f9:6:g_d0_f12:t∈Tpre
23:752:62499:0:0:248:306:265:11:g_d0_f8:11:g_d0_f2:αt·Dt·Ij+
23:753:62508:0:24:316:332:275:11:g_d0_f10:11:g_d0_f10:∑
23:754:62509:24:0:309:339:251:8:g_d0_f9:6:g_d0_f12:t∈Tpost
23:755:62516:0:35:341:525:265:11:g_d0_f8:11:g_d0_f2:αt·Dt·Ij+X′jt·γ+εjt,(1)
23:756:62539:35:19:79:525:230:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:whereyjtis the outcome variable (urbanization or log GDP per capita) in countryjat time
23:757:62626:19:18:79:525:211:11:g_d0_f8:11:g_d0_f2:t, thedt’s denote a full set of time effects, theδj’s denote a full set of country (polity) fixed
23:758:62723:18:19:79:525:193:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:effects,Xjtis a vector of other covariates, which will be included in some of the robustness
23:759:62815:19:18:79:526:174:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:checks,  andεjtis  a  disturbance  term.   The  key  variable  of  interest  for  us  is  the  treatment
23:760:62919:18:19:79:525:156:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:variableIj,  which is either a dummy denoting polities treated by the French Revolutionary
23:761:63009:19:16:79:525:137:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:armies/by Napoleon or the number of years of French occupation.  The coefficients of interest
23:762:63102:16:15:87:525:121:6:g_d0_f4:9:g_d0_f5:24Recall that for Germany the Revolutionary treatment affects only the Rhineland, which is why there are
23:763:63206:15:7:79:174:106:9:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f5:no standard deviations.
23:764:63229:7:15:87:525:99:6:g_d0_f4:9:g_d0_f5:25The  urbanization  dataset  is  balanced  except  for  Hanover  and  Bavaria  in  1700,  and  the  GDP  per  capita
23:765:63346:15:0:79:303:84:9:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f5:dataset is balanced except for Russia in 1850 and 1890.
24:766:63403:0:0:79:118:671:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:are thus
24:767:63411:0:11:122:134:679:11:g_d0_f10:11:g_d0_f10:∑
24:768:63412:11:0:134:196:668:8:g_d0_f9:11:g_d0_f2:t∈Tpreαtand
24:769:63423:0:11:200:212:679:11:g_d0_f10:11:g_d0_f10:∑
24:770:63424:11:0:211:287:668:8:g_d0_f9:11:g_d0_f13:t∈Tpost, whereT
24:771:63439:0:22:290:525:675:8:g_d0_f9:11:g_d0_f2:preis the set of years before andTpostis the set
24:772:63487:22:19:79:525:653:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:of years after treatment, which together allow us to look at both pre-trends and post-French
24:773:63579:19:0:79:227:634:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Revolution differential effects (
24:774:63612:0:11:226:238:642:11:g_d0_f10:11:g_d0_f10:∑
24:775:63613:11:15:238:525:631:8:g_d0_f9:11:g_d0_f2:t∈Tαt·Dt·Ijstands for a separate interaction for eachtin
24:776:63669:15:19:79:525:616:11:g_d0_f13:11:g_d0_f2:T).  Under our hypothesis that French occupation was ‘econometrically exogenous’, we expect
24:777:63760:19:18:79:525:597:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the coefficients{αt}t∈Tprenot to be significantly different from zero, and under our hypothesis
24:778:63855:18:19:79:524:579:11:g_d0_f2:6:g_d0_f12:that the French reforms were beneficial for long-run economic growth, we expect{αt}t∈Tpost
24:779:63945:19:18:79:147:560:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:to be positive.
24:780:63960:18:18:96:525:542:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Throughout the paper, all standard errors are robust, clustered at the country/polity level
24:781:64051:18:19:79:525:524:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:to allow for an arbitrary variance-covariance matrix capturing potential serial correlation in
24:782:64145:19:29:79:366:505:11:g_d0_f2:8:g_d0_f3:the residual error term (see Wooldridge, 2002, Chapter 7).26
24:783:64205:29:26:79:274:476:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:4.1    Main Results:  Urbanization
24:784:64239:26:18:79:525:450:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:We start in Table 4 with our preferred measure of prosperity in the 19th century, urbanization
24:785:64333:18:18:79:525:432:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:rates, as the dependent variable,yjt.  The first column uses years of French occupation as the
24:786:64427:18:19:79:525:414:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:treatment, while the second uses invaded by the French during the Revolutionary period as the
24:787:64520:19:18:79:525:395:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:treatment.  Column 3 uses invasion during the Napoleonic period as the treatment.  Finally,
24:788:64611:18:19:79:518:377:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:column 4 uses years of French presence but weights the polities by their population in 1700.
24:789:64703:19:18:96:526:358:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:The setTpostincludes the treatment years 1850 and 1900,Tprecomprises 1750 and 1800,
24:790:64786:18:19:79:526:340:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:with  1700  as  the  omitted  year.   In  column  1  we  see  that  ˆα1850=−0.236  with  a  standard
24:791:64886:19:18:79:525:321:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:error of 0.154, so that by 1850 there was a negative, though relatively small and statistically
24:792:64981:18:18:79:525:303:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:insignificant effect of years of French presence on the growth of urbanization. By 1900, however,
24:793:65078:18:19:79:525:285:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:a significant positive effect occurs. Indeed, ˆα1900= 0.899 (standard error=0.382).  Importantly,
24:794:65175:19:18:79:525:266:11:g_d0_f2:8:g_d0_f3:there is no evidence of a pre-trend favoring the treated areas.  The coefficients ˆα1750and ˆα1800
24:795:65273:18:19:79:324:248:11:g_d0_f2:8:g_d0_f3:are in fact negative, but statistically insignificant.27
24:796:65329:19:16:96:525:229:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:The patterns in columns 2 and 3, which use dummies for control by the French Revolu-
24:797:65413:16:14:87:525:213:6:g_d0_f4:9:g_d0_f5:26The Huber-White standard errors turn out to be smaller than the standard errors clustered at the coun-
24:798:65517:14:11:79:525:199:9:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f5:try/polity level in almost all cases.  So our use of the fully robust variance-covariance matrix is conservative
24:799:65629:11:11:79:525:188:9:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f5:except for the possibility that asymptotic approximations may not be valid because of the limited numbers of
24:800:65737:11:11:79:525:177:9:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f5:clusters.  As a remedy for this last possibility, we also discuss how using the alternative wild bootstrap procedure
24:801:65853:11:7:79:469:166:9:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f5:suggested by Cameron, Gelbach and Miller (2008) affects the significance levels of our estimates.
24:802:65950:7:15:87:525:159:6:g_d0_f4:9:g_d0_f5:27One concern, already mentioned in footnote 26, is that the number of clusters in Table 4 is relatively small
24:803:66060:15:11:79:525:144:9:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f5:(41 polities).  As a potential check, we also computed the significance levels for our parameter estimates using the
24:804:66176:11:11:79:525:133:9:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f5:wild bootstrap procedure (based on the t-statistics with the null hypothesis imposed) as suggested by Cameron,
24:805:66286:11:11:79:525:122:9:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f5:Gelbach and Miller (2008).  We computed the significance levels using 1000 replications.  This procedure has
24:806:66394:11:11:79:525:111:9:g_d0_f5:6:g_d0_f4:little effect on the significance levels of the results in Table 4.  For example, in column 1 the p-value for  ˆα1900
24:807:66511:11:11:79:525:100:9:g_d0_f5:6:g_d0_f4:increases slightly from 0.024 to 0.034, and the p-value of the F-test of joint significance of the coefficientsα1850
24:808:66627:11:0:79:461:89:9:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f5:andα1900changes from 0.001 to 0.008.  Similar results apply to the other estimates in Table 4.
25:809:66723:0:18:79:525:671:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:tionary armies and by Napoleon as the measure of French treatment, and in column 4, which
25:810:66812:18:19:79:525:653:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:uses weighted regressions (using population in 1750 as weights), are similar to that in column
25:811:66906:19:18:79:525:634:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:1.  We continue to find a negative and insignificant effect of being occupied by the French in
25:812:67000:18:19:79:526:616:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:1850, and a positive and significant effect in 1900.  The estimates of the coefficientα1900are
25:813:67094:19:18:79:525:597:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:not statistically significant in columns 2 and 4.  Nevertheless, in all cases, the F-test shows that
25:814:67194:18:19:79:525:579:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the 1850 and 1900 interactions are jointly significant, reflecting the fact that the differences
25:815:67290:19:18:79:490:560:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:between the 1850 and 1900 coefficients are statistically significant in all specifications.
25:816:67381:18:18:96:525:542:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:However, the pre-1800 coefficients are now larger, and in column 2 and 4, they are statis-
25:817:67471:18:19:79:525:524:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:tically significant.  This raises the possibility of potential mean reversion, which may confound
25:818:67568:19:18:79:525:505:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:our estimates.  To deal with this concern, we report results from models that explicitly allow
25:819:67662:18:19:79:279:487:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:for mean reversion in the next subsection.
25:820:67704:19:18:96:525:468:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:The quantitative effects implied by these estimates are economically large but reasonable.
25:821:67794:18:19:79:525:450:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:For example, the estimate ofα1900in column 1 implies that by 1900 countries that experienced
25:822:67886:19:18:79:525:431:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:10 years of French control had urbanization rates almost 9 percentage points higher.  This is
25:823:67979:18:18:79:525:413:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:a large effect relative to mean urbanization in 1900 which was 41.2% for the entire sample,
25:824:68070:18:19:79:525:395:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:suggesting  an  increase  of  close  to  22%  (or  half  a  standard  deviation)  in  the  urbanization
25:825:68173:19:18:79:525:376:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:rate.  The effects estimated forα1900in columns 2 and 3 using treatment dummies are also
25:826:68261:18:19:79:208:358:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:quantitatively very similar.
25:827:68289:19:18:96:525:339:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Overall, these results show no evidence of a negative effect of French occupation.  On the
25:828:68379:18:19:79:525:321:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:contrary,  they  suggest  that  polities  invaded  and  reformed  by  the  French  experienced  more
25:829:68479:19:18:79:525:302:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:rapid urbanization and economic growth after 1850.  We find it reasonable that the positive
25:830:68570:18:18:79:525:284:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:effects of the French Revolution exhibit themselves after 1850, since, as discussed in Section 2,
25:831:68667:18:19:79:525:266:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the main role of the French reforms was to remove the barriers against industrialization and
25:832:68759:19:18:79:525:247:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:industrial technology and such practices did not spread in continental Europe until the second
25:833:68853:18:29:79:194:229:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:half of the 19th century.
25:834:68878:29:26:79:176:200:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:4.2    Robustness
25:835:68895:26:18:79:525:174:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Tables 5 and 6 investigate the robustness of our initial results.  In Table 5 we re-estimate the
25:836:68991:18:19:79:525:156:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:basic model from column 1 of Table 4, focusing on years of French presence as our measure of
25:837:69083:19:18:79:525:137:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:French treatment, and add some simple covariates.  Column 1 reproduces column 1 of Table
25:838:69171:18:19:79:525:119:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:4.   In  column  2  we  add,  as  covariate  vectorXjt,  latitude  interacted  with  a  full  set  of  time
25:839:69278:19:0:79:377:100:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:dummies to allow for a time varying impact of geography (i.e.,
25:840:69340:0:12:380:392:109:11:g_d0_f10:11:g_d0_f10:∑
25:841:69341:12:0:392:525:97:8:g_d0_f9:11:g_d0_f2:tηt·Dt·latitudej).  Table 5,
26:842:69371:0:18:79:525:671:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:column 2 shows that though the interactions between latitude and time effects are statistically
26:843:69466:18:19:79:525:653:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:significant, controlling for these interactions has no effect on the estimated effects of French
26:844:69562:19:18:79:137:634:11:g_d0_f2:8:g_d0_f3:treatment.28
26:845:69574:18:19:96:526:616:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:In column 3, we include a full set of interactions between initial urbanizationyj1750and
26:846:69662:19:0:79:236:597:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the full set of year dummies (i.e.,
26:847:69697:0:11:239:251:605:11:g_d0_f10:11:g_d0_f10:∑
26:848:69698:11:15:251:525:594:8:g_d0_f9:11:g_d0_f2:tηt·Dt·yj1750, where 1750 is the first date with complete
26:849:69755:15:19:79:525:579:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:urbanization  figures  for  all  polities).   This  is  a  flexible  (and  demanding)  way  of  controlling
26:850:69862:19:18:79:525:560:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:for  any  pre-existing  trends  and  mean  reversion.   The  negative  and  sometimes  statistically
26:851:69962:18:18:79:525:542:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:significant  estimates  before  1800  shown  in  Table  4  raise  the  possibility  that  there  might  be
26:852:70068:18:19:79:525:524:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:significant  mean  reversion  in  economic  growth  during  this  era,  potentially  confounding  our
26:853:70169:19:18:79:525:505:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:estimation strategy.  Nevertheless, this flexible specification has little effect on our estimates.
26:854:70268:18:19:79:525:487:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:For example,  ˆα1900is now 0.85 (standard error= 0.396) and the interactions between initial
26:855:70360:19:18:79:412:468:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:urbanization and the year dummies are also statistically insignificant.
26:856:70431:18:19:96:525:450:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:In column 4, we include a full set of interactions between year dummies and our ‘Protestant’
26:857:70523:19:18:79:525:431:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:variable.  Several influential social scientists have argued for the importance of the Protestant
26:858:70620:18:18:79:525:413:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:work ethic in causing or at least facilitating industrialization (e.g., Weber, 1905, Landes, 1998).
26:859:70719:18:19:79:525:395:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Although  there  is  some  evidence  of  differential  growth  of  Protestant  countries  (the  set  of
26:860:70822:19:18:79:525:376:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:interactions between Protestantism and the time dummies is significant at the 5% level), the
26:861:70914:18:19:79:525:358:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:inclusion  of  this  set  of  covariates  only  strengthens  the  differential  growth  effect  of  French
26:862:71020:19:18:79:525:339:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:treatment.  Column 5 finally includes all of these interactions jointly.  Our estimates are again
26:863:71117:18:19:79:166:321:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:largely unaffected.
26:864:71136:19:18:96:525:302:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:In  Table  6  we  conduct  a  variety  of  other  robustness  checks  again  restricting  attention
26:865:71235:18:18:79:525:284:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:to  years  of  French  presence  as  our  measure  of  French  treatment.   In  column  1  for  ease  of
26:866:71339:18:19:79:525:266:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:comparison we again reproduce the regression from column 1 of Table 4.  In the second column
26:867:71431:19:18:79:525:247:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:we drop the United Kingdom, since the British were the industrial leader at the time and their
26:868:71525:18:19:79:525:229:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:industrialization trajectory may have been unaffected by the French Revolution. This again has
26:869:71619:19:18:79:525:210:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:little impact on our results;  ˆα1900is now estimated to be slightly larger and highly significant.
26:870:71718:18:19:79:525:192:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Eastern Europe,  where serfdom was more widespread,  may also be a poor control for more
26:871:71806:19:18:79:525:173:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:western areas.  Motivated by this reasoning, in column 3 we drop both the United Kingdom
26:872:71894:18:18:79:525:155:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:and Eastern  Europe.  The basic  pattern remains  unchanged,  though with  a slightly smaller
26:873:71987:18:16:79:525:137:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:coefficient  ˆα1900.  In column 4,  we drop Germany and Italy,  as a preparation for the results
26:874:72083:16:15:87:525:121:6:g_d0_f4:9:g_d0_f5:28As with the results in Table 4, those in Tables 5 and 6 are robust to using the wild bootstrap procedure
26:875:72189:15:11:79:525:106:9:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f5:to compute p-values, and our estimates remain significant at conventional levels.  For example, using the same
26:876:72299:11:11:79:525:95:9:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f5:procedure as in footnote 27, the p-value for  ˆα1900in column 2 changes from 0.025 to 0.028, and the p-value of
26:877:72410:11:0:79:460:84:9:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f5:the F-test of joint significance of the coefficientsα1850andα1900increases from 0.001 to 0.014.
27:878:72507:0:18:79:525:671:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:using Maddison’s data, where we cannot distinguish across German and Italian sub-national
27:879:72596:18:19:79:525:653:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:polities.  In this case, the qualitative pattern of the results is similar, but ˆα1900is much smaller
27:880:72697:19:18:79:525:634:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:and statistically insignificant.  This already constitutes a warning about the interpretation of
27:881:72793:18:19:79:525:616:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the results using Maddison’s GDP estimates, where we will lose all of the within Germany and
27:882:72885:19:18:79:150:597:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Italy variation.
27:883:72901:18:19:96:525:579:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:The remaining columns of Table 6, allow for mean reversion using the alternative strategy
27:884:72990:19:18:79:525:560:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:of  explicitly  introducing  the  lagged  dependent  variable  on  the  right-hand  side.   To  ensure
27:885:73092:18:18:79:525:542:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:consistency,  these models are estimated using the Generalized Method of Moments (GMM)
27:886:73178:18:19:79:525:524:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:strategy suggested by Arellano and Bond (1991).  The results are generally similar to the OLS
27:887:73271:19:18:79:525:505:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:estimates without the lagged dependent variable and the lagged dependent variable itself is
27:888:73362:18:19:79:139:487:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:insignificant.
27:889:73376:19:18:96:525:468:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Also noteworthy is that in all of these specifications, we do not find evidence of pre-trends
27:890:73469:18:19:79:525:450:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:favoring areas subsequently occupied by the French.  We find this reassuring for our overall
27:891:73561:19:29:79:167:431:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:empirical strategy.
27:892:73580:29:25:79:287:402:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:4.3    Results with GDP Per Capita
27:893:73614:25:19:79:525:377:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Table  7  reports  estimates  of  equation  (1)  using  GDP  per  capita  as  the  dependent  variable.
27:894:73717:19:18:79:525:358:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:The baseline specification, reported in columns 1, 2, and 3, excludes Italy and Germany, since
27:895:73811:18:18:79:525:340:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:these  countries  comprise  both  treated  and  untreated  sub-national  polities.   In  addition,  the
27:896:73914:18:19:79:525:322:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:setTpre(for the pre-trend specification tests) now includes 1700 and 1820 (even though there
27:897:74006:19:18:79:525:303:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:may already be some effect in 1820), whileTpostincludes 1850, 1870, 1890 and 1900.  With all
27:898:74098:18:19:79:525:285:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:three measures of French treatment, there is no evidence of significant effects before 1850.  The
27:899:74195:19:18:79:525:266:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:coefficients for 1850 and thereafter are all positive and individually statistically significant in
27:900:74294:18:19:79:525:248:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:columns 1 and 2.  In column 3, where we use the dummy variable for control by Napoleon, the
27:901:74385:19:18:79:525:229:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:effects are not statistically significant.29The quantitative magnitudes of the estimates are also
27:902:74482:18:18:79:525:211:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:similar to the results with urbanization rates.  For example, the estimate of ˆα1900in column 2,
27:903:74578:18:19:79:525:193:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:0.359, implies that by 1900 countries that were occupied by the French Revolutionary armies
27:904:74669:19:18:79:508:174:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:would have reached about 36% higher per capita income relative to unoccupied countries.
27:905:74756:18:19:96:525:156:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:The remainder of Table 7 focuses on the measure of years of French presence and reports
27:906:74843:19:16:79:525:137:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:specifications that also include Italy and Germany (column 4), excludes the United Kingdom
27:907:74933:16:15:87:525:121:6:g_d0_f4:9:g_d0_f5:29However, in contrast to the results in Tables 4-6, the statistical significance of the estimates in this table is
27:908:75048:15:11:79:525:106:9:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f5:not robust to using bootstrapped p-values.  Typically, the p-value of the F-statistic resulting from a test of joint
27:909:75164:11:11:79:525:95:9:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f5:significance of all post-1820 coefficients increases to approximately 0.5 and is thus highly insignificant.  This
27:910:75277:11:0:79:414:84:9:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f5:suggests that the results using GDP per capita should be interpreted with caution.
28:911:75361:0:18:79:525:671:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:(column 5), also excludes Eastern Europe (column 6) and includes a full set of latitude, Protes-
28:912:75457:18:19:79:525:653:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:tant an initial GDP time interactions (column 7).  The overall pattern is similar.  None of the
28:913:75552:19:18:79:525:634:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:specifications show statistically significant differential effects before 1850, and all specifications
28:914:75654:18:19:79:525:616:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:show positive effects after (and including) 1850.  While individual coefficients are insignificant
28:915:75752:19:18:79:525:597:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:in many specifications, the F- tests for the joint significance of all post-1820 interactions (1850
28:916:75851:18:19:79:525:579:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:onwards) in all cases indicate that there is significantly faster growth in countries occupied by
28:917:75948:19:18:79:184:560:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the French after 1850.
28:918:75970:18:18:96:525:542:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:In sum,  results using Maddison’s GDP estimates also show no evidence that the French
28:919:76055:18:19:79:525:524:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:evolution have negative economic consequences.  In fact, the estimates show a positive effect of
28:920:76151:19:18:79:525:505:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the French revolution, particularly after 1850 (though this is less robust than the results with
28:921:76247:18:19:79:525:487:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:urbanization).  As we mentioned in the Introduction,  however,  using this GDP data entails
28:922:76338:19:18:79:525:468:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:discarding a considerable amount of variation in treatment, which comes from the within Italy
28:923:76431:18:19:79:525:450:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:and within Germany experiences.  This is the reason why we have emphasized the urbanization
28:924:76522:19:34:79:257:431:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:data as our main dependent variable.
28:925:76558:34:29:79:284:397:14:g_d0_f1:14:g_d0_f1:5    Within-German Evidence
28:926:76585:29:19:79:525:368:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:The results so far indicate that countries where the French Revolution imposed radical insti-
28:927:76678:19:18:79:525:349:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:tutional reforms,  such as the abolition of feudal land relations and the power of the guilds,
28:928:76772:18:18:79:525:331:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:experienced faster growth in the second half of the 19th century, particularly after the industri-
28:929:76870:18:19:79:525:313:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:alization process got underway in earnest in continental Europe.  We now look at the variation
28:930:76964:19:18:79:525:294:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:within  Germany,  which  is  useful  for  several  reasons.   First,  it  will  enable  us  to  focus  on  a
28:931:77072:18:19:79:525:276:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:sample of polities that were more homogeneous than the whole set of European countries at
28:932:77161:19:18:79:525:257:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the turn of the 19th century.  Second, the greater availability of data will allow us to pinpoint
28:933:77258:18:19:79:525:239:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:more precisely when in the second part of the 19th century the divergence between occupied
28:934:77348:19:18:79:525:220:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:and unoccupied areas may have started.  Finally and most importantly, we will be able to use
28:935:77440:18:18:79:525:202:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:detailed data on institutional reforms and other outcome variables to further investigate the
28:936:77533:18:30:79:378:184:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:implications of the reforms imposed by the French Revolution.
28:937:77594:30:25:79:243:154:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:5.1    Reduced-Form Results
28:938:77621:25:19:79:525:129:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:We first examine reduced-form models similar to those estimated in Tables 4-6, but for the 8
28:939:77713:19:18:79:525:110:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:German polities for which we have urbanization data.  Our estimating equation is identical to
28:940:77806:18:0:79:526:92:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:(1), withyjtagain corresponding to the urbanization rate, but now defined for to sub-national
29:941:77901:0:18:79:525:671:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:German polities.  The rest of the variables are defined similarly to those in equation (1):  the
29:942:77997:18:19:79:526:653:11:g_d0_f8:11:g_d0_f2:dt’s denote a full set of time effects, theδj’s denote a full set of city effects,Xjtis a vector
29:943:78093:19:18:79:525:634:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:of other covariates,  andεjtis the error term.  The dummyIjis again the treatment status
29:944:78181:18:19:79:229:616:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:defined in the same three ways.
29:945:78212:19:18:96:525:597:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Our baseline sample now consists of the years 1700,  1750,  1800,  1850,  1875,  1880,  1885,
29:946:78305:18:19:79:525:579:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:1890, 1895, 1900, 1905 and 1910; we are thus able to take advantage of the richer information
29:947:78398:19:18:79:525:560:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:we have about urbanization within Germany as compared to the rest of Europe.  We take the
29:948:78487:18:18:79:525:542:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:setTpostto consist of the years between 1850 and 1910, while the setTpre(for the pre-trend
29:949:78577:18:19:79:442:524:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:specification check) consists of 1750 and 1800.  1700 is the omitted category.
29:950:78655:19:18:96:525:505:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:The estimates from the baseline models are reported in Table 8.  The first column uses years
29:951:78747:18:19:79:525:487:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:of French presence as the treatment.  There is again no evidence of differential growth before
29:952:78841:19:18:79:525:468:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:1850:   ˆα1750and  ˆα1800are  small  and  statistically  significant.   In  contrast,  ˆα1850is  positive,
29:953:78947:18:19:79:525:450:11:g_d0_f2:8:g_d0_f3:though insignificant.  By 1875 there is a statistically significant effect of treatment with  ˆα1875
29:954:79047:19:18:79:525:431:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:equal to 0.71 (standard error= 0.20). In addition, the differential growth continues thereafter so
29:955:79145:18:18:79:525:413:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:that by 1910 we have  ˆα1910= 1.07 (standard error= 0.37).  This indicates that the differential
29:956:79241:18:19:79:525:395:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:effects of French treatment start relatively early in the second part of the 19th century (certainly
29:957:79341:19:18:79:525:376:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:well before 1900).  Quantitative magnitudes are comparable as well, but somewhat larger than
29:958:79433:18:19:79:526:358:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:those from the cross-country estimates.  For example, the coefficient of  ˆα1900= 0.99 indicates
29:959:79529:19:18:79:525:339:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:that  a  polity  that  experienced  10  years  of  French  control,  on  average,  achieved  about  10
29:960:79631:18:19:79:408:321:11:g_d0_f2:8:g_d0_f3:percentage points higher urbanization relative to unoccupied areas.30
29:961:79700:19:18:96:525:302:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:In column 2 we use invasion of Revolutionary armies as our measure of French treatment.
29:962:79787:18:18:79:525:284:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Recall that in the German context, this is simply testing for differential growth of urbanization
29:963:79884:18:19:79:525:266:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:in the Rhineland versus the rest of Germany.  The pattern here is similar to that in column
29:964:79975:19:18:79:525:247:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:1, with the estimated effect becoming significant in 1875, the size of the coefficient increasing
29:965:80072:18:19:79:525:229:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:over time and the significance level remaining high.  In column 3 we use the dummy variable
29:966:80163:19:18:79:394:210:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:for occupation by Napoleon; the results are again broadly similar.
29:967:80229:18:19:96:525:192:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:In column 4, we use the years of French control measure and exclude the part of Prussia
29:968:80316:19:18:79:525:173:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:that was not incorporated into Napoleon’s satellite kingdom, which lies for the most part east
29:969:80410:18:18:79:525:155:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:of the Elbe.  This is a useful check since the eastern German areas with stronger feudal labor
29:970:80504:18:16:79:525:137:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:relations may be less comparable to, and thus are worse control, for polities occupied by the
29:971:80597:16:15:87:525:121:6:g_d0_f4:9:g_d0_f5:30As  in  Table  7  (and  in  contrast  to  Tables  4-6),  these  results  are  not  robust  to  using  wild  bootstrapped
29:972:80719:15:11:79:525:106:9:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f5:significance  levels.   For  example,  in  column  1,  the  p-value  for  the  test  of  joint  significance  of  all  post-1800
29:973:80847:11:0:79:245:95:9:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f5:coefficients increases from 0.000 to 0.360.
30:974:80892:0:18:79:525:671:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:French.  In the event, the results in column 4 are very similar to those in column 1 and indicate
30:975:80989:18:19:79:474:653:11:g_d0_f2:8:g_d0_f3:that our findings are not given by a comparison of the west and east of the Elbe.31
30:976:81072:19:18:96:525:634:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Columns  5-7  focus  on  the  years  of  French  control  measure  and  include  interactions  of
30:977:81169:18:19:79:525:616:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Protestant, latitude and initial urbanization with linear time trends, while column 8 weights
30:978:81262:19:18:79:525:597:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the data by population in 1700.  The results are similar to those in column 1.  Finally, column 9
30:979:81359:18:19:79:525:579:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:reports results from a specification including a lagged dependent variable. For this specification,
30:980:81458:19:18:79:525:560:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:we only include the years 1700, 1750, 1800, 1850, 1900, to obtain a panel dataset with evenly
30:981:81551:18:18:79:442:542:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:spaced time intervals.  The estimates are again similar to those in column 1.
30:982:81628:18:19:96:525:524:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Overall, the evidence in Table 8 is consistent with that presented in the previous sections.
30:983:81720:19:18:79:525:505:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:In fact, the effects of French treatment are somewhat more precisely estimated, and because we
30:984:81814:18:19:79:525:487:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:have more frequent observations, we can see the effects occur as early as 1875.  We conclude, in
30:985:81910:19:18:79:525:468:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:line with our results from the previous section, that there is no evidence of a negative economic
30:986:82007:18:19:79:525:450:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:impact of the French Revolution; on the contrary, there is considerable evidence indicating that
30:987:82103:19:29:79:523:431:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:areas occupied by the French grew considerably faster in the second half of the 19th century.
30:988:82196:29:25:79:365:402:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:5.2    Instrumental-Variables Models in Germany
30:989:82243:25:18:79:525:377:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:One  advantage  of  our  within  Germany  analysis  is  that  we  can  verify  the  impact  of  French
30:990:82345:18:19:79:525:359:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:treatment on institutional reforms and then also estimate models where all of the effects of
30:991:82437:19:18:79:525:340:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:French  occupation  are  assumed  to  work  through  institutions.   In  particular,  we  posit  the
30:992:82537:18:28:79:525:322:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:following simple relationship between our index of institutional reform and French occupation:
30:993:82631:28:28:211:525:294:11:g_d0_f8:11:g_d0_f2:Rjt=dt+δj+ψ·t·Tt>1800·Ij+ηjt,(2)
30:994:82663:28:19:79:525:266:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:whereRjtis  the  value  of  the  reform  index  for  polityjin  Germany  at  timet,  which  was
30:995:82758:19:18:79:526:247:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:introduced in the context of Table 1 above.dtandδjare time effects and polity fixed effects
30:996:82849:18:19:79:525:229:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:and as usualIjis our treatment variable, which in this section we take to be years of French
30:997:82941:19:18:79:525:210:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:presence.ηjtis a disturbance term.  The variableTt>1800is a dummy for post-1800 dates, so
30:998:83030:18:16:79:524:192:11:g_d0_f2:8:g_d0_f3:thatt·Tt>1800is a linear time trend that turns on after 1800 (and is equal to 0 before then).32
30:999:83125:16:15:87:525:176:6:g_d0_f4:9:g_d0_f5:31The results including the areas East of the Elbe are useful, on the other hand, because they provide evidence
30:1000:83236:15:11:79:525:161:9:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f5:against a related but different hypothesis that part of the effects of French occupation within Germany are partly
30:1001:83350:11:11:79:525:150:9:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f5:(or largely) due to defensive modernization efforts of Prussia (itself triggered by the French Revolution).  After
30:1002:83464:11:11:79:525:139:9:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f5:the Congress of Vienna in 1815, Prussia took over large parts of Napoleonic Western Germany including the
30:1003:83569:11:11:79:525:128:9:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f5:Rhineland and Westphalia.  As noted in footnote 17, this is part of the explanation for why institutional reforms
30:1004:83682:11:11:79:525:117:9:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f5:were not reversed in Germany after Napoleon’s fall.  Nevertheless, our interpretation is that the within-Germany
30:1005:83794:11:11:79:525:106:9:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f5:results are unlikely to be due to such a Prussian effect.  First, the general pattern is similar for the whole of
30:1006:83907:11:7:79:382:95:9:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f5:Europe.  Second, in Germany much of Prussia is itself in the control group.
30:1007:83982:7:0:87:381:88:6:g_d0_f4:9:g_d0_f5:32To simplify the interpretation of coefficients, timetis divided by 1000.
31:1008:84058:0:18:79:525:671:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:We start with this simpler form in (2), because in the second stage we are interested in the
31:1009:84150:18:19:79:525:653:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:main effect of institutional reforms and thus using a full set of time interactions as instruments
31:1010:84248:19:18:79:525:634:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:might exaggerate the strength of our first-stage relationship.  We return to a specification in
31:1011:84343:18:19:79:481:616:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:which the full set of time interactions are used in the first stage in columns 3 and 4.
31:1012:84430:19:29:96:233:597:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:The second-stage equation is
31:1013:84458:29:29:236:525:568:11:g_d0_f8:11:g_d0_f2:yjt=dt+δj+φ·Rjt+υjt,(3)
31:1014:84481:29:19:79:438:539:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:whereyjtis urbanization,dtandδjare time effects and polity fixed effects.
31:1015:84554:19:18:96:525:520:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Table 9 shows the results of estimating (3) using OLS and two-stage least squares.  Column
31:1016:84644:18:19:79:525:502:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:1 is for the entire Germany using years of French presence as the measure of French treatment.
31:1017:84738:19:18:79:525:483:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Panel  A  shows  estimates  (3)  using  OLS  for  comparison.   The  reforms  index  has  a  positive
31:1018:84839:18:18:79:525:465:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:and statistically significant effect on urbanization with an estimated coefficient ofˆφ= 0.368
31:1019:84933:18:19:79:187:447:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:(standard error=0.13).
31:1020:84955:19:18:96:525:428:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Panel B depicts estimates of equation (2).  It shows a strong first stage with the coefficient
31:1021:85049:18:19:79:525:410:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:on  the  interaction  between  the  post  dummy  and  years  of  French  presence  beingˆψ=  0.711
31:1022:85147:19:18:79:525:391:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:(standard  error=0.25).   The  strong  first-stage  relationship  indicates  that  even  though  there
31:1023:85249:18:18:79:525:373:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:were reforms in German areas not occupied by the French (most likely due to defensive mod-
31:1024:85339:18:19:79:525:355:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:ernization as in Baden and in Prussia), occupation by the French was a significant determinant
31:1025:85433:19:18:79:126:336:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:of reform.
31:1026:85443:18:19:96:525:318:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Panel C reports the second stage.  These results show that the impact of reforms on urban-
31:1027:85533:19:18:79:525:299:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:ization is also highly significant, now with a larger coefficientˆφ= 0.658 (standard error=0.21).
31:1028:85630:18:19:79:525:281:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:The greater magnitude of this coefficient is not surprising in view of the fact that the OLS
31:1029:85722:19:18:79:525:262:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:coefficient is likely to be subject to considerable attenuation, both because the extent of re-
31:1030:85817:18:18:79:525:244:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:form is measured with error and also because, conceptually, our reforms are only proxies for a
31:1031:85911:18:19:79:525:226:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:broader range of institutional reforms undertaken during this era.33Column 2 repeats these
31:1032:86001:19:18:79:490:207:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:regressions excluding the East of the Elbe and shows very similar results to column 1.
31:1033:86087:18:19:96:525:189:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Columns  3  and  4  reestimate  the  same  models  as  in  columns  1  and  2,  but  instead  of  a
31:1034:86186:19:18:79:525:170:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:linear interaction of time with years of French presence in the first stage, they include a full
31:1035:86282:18:19:79:525:152:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:set of interactions between post-1800 dummies and years of French presence (as in equation
31:1036:86372:19:18:79:525:133:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:(1)).  We do not show the corresponding first stages in Panel B to save space.  This exercise
31:1037:86465:18:16:79:525:115:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:is  useful  for  two  reasons.   First,  the  very  similar  coefficients  in  columns  3  and  4  show  that
31:1038:86574:16:15:87:525:99:6:g_d0_f4:9:g_d0_f5:33The results in this table are weakened by the use of the wild bootstrap-t method, with the level of significance
31:1039:86688:15:0:79:299:84:9:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f5:forˆφtypically increasing to around or just above 10%.
32:1040:86744:0:18:79:525:671:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:using the linear time interaction in (2) is not important for our results.  Second, because with
32:1041:86840:18:19:79:525:653:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:this specification we have more instruments than endogenous regressors,  we can perform an
32:1042:86930:19:18:79:525:634:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:overidentification test of the validity of the instruments.  Economically, this amounts to testing
32:1043:87028:18:19:79:525:616:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:whether we can reject the hypothesis that all of the effects of the post-1800 time interactions
32:1044:87123:19:18:79:525:597:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:with French occupation work through the reforms index. To perform the overidentification test,
32:1045:87217:18:19:79:525:579:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:we use the Huber-White variance-covariance matrix without clustering, since this corresponds
32:1046:87309:19:18:79:525:560:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:to smaller standard errors and thus stacks the cards against our hypothesis.  The results show
32:1047:87403:18:18:79:525:542:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:that the overidentification tests are very far from rejecting the above-mentioned hypothesis.
32:1048:87496:18:19:79:525:524:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:This gives some support to our interpretation that French occupation impacted urbanization
32:1049:87586:19:18:79:525:505:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:and economic growth in German polities in the second half of the 19th century mainly through
32:1050:87678:18:19:79:257:487:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the reforms that the French imposed.
32:1051:87714:19:18:96:525:468:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Columns 5-8 include interactions between Protestant, latitude and initial organization and
32:1052:87804:18:19:79:525:450:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:linear time trends (these models again only include a linear interaction of time with years of
32:1053:87898:19:18:79:525:431:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:French presence in the first stage, as in (2)).  These controls have little effect on the results.
32:1054:87996:18:18:79:525:413:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Finally,  column  8  reports  weighted  regressions,  again  showing  a  very  similar  pattern  to  the
32:1055:88100:18:19:79:173:395:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:results in column 1.
32:1056:88120:19:18:96:525:376:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Overall the results in this section are consistent with our interpretation that occupation by
32:1057:88213:18:19:79:525:358:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the French induced significant institutional reforms and these reforms paved the way for more
32:1058:88306:19:28:79:433:339:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:rapid economic growth particularly in the second half of the 19th century.
32:1059:88380:28:26:79:312:311:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:5.3    Other German Outcome Variables
32:1060:88417:26:18:79:525:285:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Our focus so far on urbanization rates and GDP per-capita was driven by our desire to check
32:1061:88508:18:19:79:525:267:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:for pre-trends—both of these variables allowed us to see whether there were differential changes
32:1062:88604:19:18:79:525:248:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:before the French Revolution.  The lack of such pre-trends so far motivates us to look at other
32:1063:88699:18:19:79:525:230:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:proxies for economic growth and industrialization in the 19th century.  More specifically, we
32:1064:88792:19:18:79:525:211:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:focus on the length of railway tracks in the area and the sectoral composition of employment,
32:1065:88885:18:18:79:501:193:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:which are available for German administrative units in the 19th century, but not before.
32:1066:88973:18:19:96:525:175:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Given  the  absence  of  pre-French  Revolution  data,  we  adopt  a  simpler  strategy  in  this
32:1067:89070:19:27:79:422:156:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:subsection.  We report a series of cross-sectional regressions of the form:
32:1068:89145:27:26:250:525:129:11:g_d0_f8:11:g_d0_f2:yjt=dt+αt·Ij+εjt(4)
32:1069:89164:26:19:79:525:103:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:for eacht.  Hereyjtis again the outcome variable (railways or sectoral shares) in districtjat
32:1070:89257:19:0:79:525:84:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:timet,dtnow denotes a year-specific constant,Ijagain represents years of French presence
33:1071:89347:0:18:79:525:671:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:in districtj,εjtis a disturbance term, andαt’s are the coefficients of interest.  In particular,
33:1072:89443:18:19:79:484:653:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:changes inαt’s can be interpreted as differential growth related to French treatment.
33:1073:89528:19:18:96:525:634:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Data on railways construction are available at the level of districts (Regierungsbezirke).  In
33:1074:89622:18:19:79:525:616:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:our dataset, districts have an average size of 12,000 square km and a population of 1.15 million
33:1075:89718:19:18:79:525:597:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:inhabitants.  Data until 1874 are available only for Prussia, from 1880 onwards for the entirety
33:1076:89814:18:19:79:525:579:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:of the German Empire.  There are 35 districts in Prussia, 38 in the rest of Germany.  We are
33:1077:89906:19:18:79:502:560:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:thus able to look at railways in the years 1859, 1864, 1869, 1874, 1880, 1885, 1890, 1895.
33:1078:89996:18:18:96:525:542:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Table 10 shows the results of estimating equation (4) with the left-hand side variable as log
33:1079:90089:18:19:79:525:524:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:kilometers of railways in districtj.  The regressions for 1859, 1864, 1869, and 1874, show no
33:1080:90182:19:18:79:525:505:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:significant differences in railway tracks by years of French presence both in the entire Germany
33:1081:90278:18:19:79:525:487:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:and in the West of the Elbe.  However, by 1880 (after the non-Prussian districts are added to
33:1082:90371:19:18:79:525:468:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the dataset) we find significantly more railway tracks in areas occupied by the French.  These
33:1083:90465:18:19:79:525:450:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:differences are confirmed in subsequent periods, particularly when attention is confined to the
33:1084:90560:19:18:79:162:431:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:West of the Elbe.
33:1085:90577:18:18:96:525:413:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Table 11 turns to the sectoral shares of employment.  Economic progress in the 19th century
33:1086:90668:18:19:79:525:395:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:was associated with a move out of agricultural activities and into the industrial and manufac-
33:1087:90762:19:18:79:525:376:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:turing sectors.  We exploit variation across districts in sectoral shares of employment, based on
33:1088:90859:18:19:79:525:358:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:data assembled by Frank (1994) for four points in time:  1849, 1882, 1895, and 1907.  The re-
33:1089:90952:19:18:79:525:339:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:sults in Table 11 show that by 1849 there was already less agriculture and greater industry and
33:1090:91047:18:19:79:525:321:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:manufacturing employment in areas occupied by the French, though these differences are not
33:1091:91137:19:18:79:525:302:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:statistically significant.  They become larger and statistically significant by 1882 and remain so
33:1092:91235:18:18:79:525:284:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:until 1908.  This evidence therefore also suggests that there was more rapid industrialization
33:1093:91329:18:35:79:521:266:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:in areas that underwent more significant reforms because of French occupation and invasion.
33:1094:91420:35:29:79:180:231:14:g_d0_f1:14:g_d0_f1:6    Conclusion
33:1095:91435:29:18:79:525:202:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:The French Revolution of 1789 had a momentous impact on France and its neighboring coun-
33:1096:91523:18:19:79:525:184:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:tries.  The Revolution violently toppled the established regime and started a complex process,
33:1097:91617:19:18:79:525:165:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:involving both the infamous FrenchTerrorand also radical institutional changes, including the
33:1098:91710:18:19:79:525:147:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:abolition of the remnants of feudalism in agriculture, the reduction of the power of the nobility
33:1099:91807:19:18:79:525:128:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:and the clergy, the abolition of guilds and internal tariffs, and the declaration of equality before
33:1100:91907:18:19:79:188:110:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the law for all citizens.
33:1101:91932:19:0:96:525:91:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:More importantly for the focus of this paper, the French Revolutionary armies, and later
34:1102:92022:0:18:79:525:671:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Napoleon, invaded and controlled Belgium, the Netherlands, Italy, Switzerland, parts of Ger-
34:1103:92114:18:19:79:525:653:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:many.  In all of these places, the Revolution undertook essentially the same radical political,
34:1104:92209:19:18:79:525:634:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:legal,  and  economic  reforms  as  in  France.   However,  invasion  by  the  French  Revolutionary
34:1105:92309:18:19:79:525:616:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:armies  (and  later  by  Napoleon)  also  came  with  chaos  and  the  exploitation  of  the  occupied
34:1106:92411:19:18:79:129:597:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:territories.
34:1107:92423:18:19:96:525:579:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Despite the very large literature on the causes and consequences of the French Revolution,
34:1108:92513:19:18:79:525:560:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:there has been little investigation into the long-run implications of the institutional changes
34:1109:92608:18:18:79:525:542:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:brought about by the French Revolution.  This paper is an attempt in this direction and it
34:1110:92698:18:19:79:525:524:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:investigates the implications of the radical institutional reforms imposed by the French armies
34:1111:92793:19:18:79:345:505:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:on neighboring countries as a quasi-natural experiment.
34:1112:92848:18:19:96:525:487:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:The evidence suggests that areas that underwent the institutional reforms of the French
34:1113:92935:19:18:79:525:468:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Revolution experienced more rapid urbanization, especially after 1850.  This pattern is fairly
34:1114:93029:18:19:79:525:450:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:robust when we look at cross-country data on urbanization and if anything stronger when we
34:1115:93119:19:18:79:525:431:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:focus on within-Germany  variation.  Even though it is  much less  satisfactory for examining
34:1116:93212:18:18:79:525:413:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:these issues, when we use Maddison’s data on GDP the overall pattern is similar, though the
34:1117:93303:18:19:79:218:395:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:results are somewhat weaker.
34:1118:93331:19:18:96:525:376:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:These findings are interesting not only as a historical appraisal of the economic impacts of
34:1119:93423:18:19:79:525:358:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the Revolution but more importantly because of their implications for the role of institutions
34:1120:93517:19:18:79:525:339:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:in economic development and for the debate about sources of institutional change.  The his-
34:1121:93608:18:19:79:525:321:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:torical experience we have studied is a clear example of a large-scale and radical institutional
34:1122:93704:19:18:79:525:302:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:change.  In this light, our findings support recent empirical work emphasizing the centrality of
34:1123:93800:18:18:79:525:284:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:institutional differences for comparative economic development.  More importantly, the results
34:1124:93894:18:19:79:525:266:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:are  inconsistent  with  influential  theses  in  social  sciences  emphasizing  the  potential  negative
34:1125:93999:19:18:79:525:247:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:effects of the French Revolution because it imposed potentially ‘inappropriate,’ ‘designed’ and
34:1126:94094:18:19:79:525:229:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:‘French’ institutions in a ‘Big Bang’ style—all of these often argued to be inimical to economic
34:1127:94190:19:18:79:525:210:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:progress.  On the contrary, the evidence supports our hypothesis that the institutions of the
34:1128:94283:18:19:79:525:192:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f2:ancien  r ́egimeimpeded prosperity,  and that the radical institutional reforms removed these
34:1129:94376:19:18:79:525:173:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:barriers and paved the way for industrialization and economic growth.  Naturally, all of these
34:1130:94470:18:18:79:525:155:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:findings have to be interpreted with caution, both because our analysis was limited to the avail-
34:1131:94567:18:19:79:525:137:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:able historical data and results from one historical episode cannot always be extrapolated to
34:1132:94660:19:18:79:525:118:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:other eras.  Nevertheless, it is noteworthy that our findings do suggest that radical institutional
34:1133:94759:18:0:79:502:100:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:reforms can have long-run beneficial consequences, at least in certain historical contexts.

41:1322:106522:0:29:79:461:671:14:g_d0_f1:14:g_d0_f1:Appendix B: Coding Urbanization in German Polities
41:1323:106572:29:19:79:525:642:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:In  this  paper,  we  use  urbanization  rates  (defined  as  the  ratio  of  population  living  in  cities
41:1324:106680:19:18:79:525:623:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:above  5,000  inhabitants  over  total  population)  for  a  selection  of  eight  pre-unitary  German
41:1325:106782:18:19:79:525:605:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:polities:  Hanover, the Rhine province of Prussia, the Westphalian province of Prussia, the rest
41:1326:106878:19:18:79:525:586:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:of Prussia,  excluding the far Eastern provinces of East and West Prussia,34Saxony,  Baden,
41:1327:106969:18:18:79:211:568:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:W ̈urttemberg, and Bavaria.
41:1328:106996:18:19:96:525:550:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:The definition of these regions follows post-1815 borders. So, for example, Saxony comprises
41:1329:107088:19:18:79:525:531:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:only  the  part  left  after  its  substantial  territorial  losses  in  the  Congress  of  Vienna,  Hanover
41:1330:107196:18:19:79:525:513:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:comprises East Frisia, Hildesheim, etc., and Bavaria comprises Franconia (but not the Bavarian
41:1331:107290:19:18:79:525:494:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Palatinate and the territories later lost to Austria,  theHausruckvierteland theInnviertel).
41:1332:107382:18:19:79:525:476:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:For the period before 1800, we have resorted to available evidence on population growth rates
41:1333:107475:19:18:79:525:457:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:in territorial units that roughly corresponded to these post-1815 states, and we have used these
41:1334:107571:18:18:79:525:439:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:rates to project total population numbers back from 1800.  In two cases, Hanover and Bavaria,
41:1335:107664:18:19:79:525:421:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the available evidence on population growth rates from 1700 to 1750 was too weak as to allow
41:1336:107756:19:18:79:525:402:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:us to construct an estimate of total population in 1700.  Further details on the construction of
41:1337:107852:18:19:79:243:384:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the series are available on request.
41:1338:107888:19:18:96:525:365:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:The total number of people living in cities above 5,000 inhabitants has been computed from
41:1339:107978:18:29:79:286:347:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the Bairoch, Batou, Ch`evre (1988) dataset.

42:1376:110484:19:18:79:525:220:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:in the fact that these were sovereign states (e.g., Tuscany), in other cases we had to break up

42:1378:110675:18:19:79:525:184:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:parts); in the case of the Emilian states, we chose to aggregate two small states that shared
42:1379:110768:19:18:79:267:165:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:an analogous experience of French rule.
42:1380:110807:18:19:96:525:147:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:For some periods, we had to adjust our estimates taking into account border changes that
42:1381:110895:19:18:79:525:128:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:occurred  between  the  18th  and  the  19th  century,  for  example  in  the  case  of  the  Lomellina
42:1382:110998:18:19:79:525:110:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:(changing hands between Lombardy and Piedmont), or the duchy of Lucca (from Modena to
42:1383:111083:19:0:79:125:91:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Tuscany).
43:1384:111094:0:18:96:526:671:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Urbanization rates were constructed by dividing the total urban population as from Bairoch,
43:1385:111185:18:30:79:344:653:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Batou, Ch`evre (1988) with the total population figures.

44:1412:113011:0:29:79:400:671:14:g_d0_f1:14:g_d0_f1:Appendix D: Coding Urbanization after 1850
44:1413:113053:29:19:79:525:642:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:For urbanization rates in 1900 we resorted, where possible, to official census data detailing the
44:1414:113150:19:18:79:525:623:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:size of the population living in urban centers above 5000 inhabitants.  These were available
44:1415:113242:18:19:79:525:605:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:for the following countries:  Germany (including data referring to pre-unitary territorial units),
44:1416:113340:19:18:79:525:586:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Italy (including data referring to pre-unitary territorial units), Italy, France, Belgium, England
44:1417:113438:18:18:79:131:568:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:and Wales.
44:1418:113448:18:19:96:525:550:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:For the remaining countries the urbanization rate was computed by adding up the total
44:1419:113533:19:18:79:525:531:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:population residing in cities above 5000 inhabitants from Lahmeyer (populstat.info), and di-
44:1420:113625:18:19:79:525:513:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:viding this figure by the total population of a country in its present-day borders.  The latter
44:1421:113720:19:18:79:525:494:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:is obtained either from McEvedy and Jones (1978),  Lahmeyer (populstat.info) or Maddison
44:1422:113808:18:19:79:112:476:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:(2003).
44:1423:113815:19:18:96:525:457:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Additionally,  in  the  case  of  German  pre-unitarian  territories,  we  could  construct  exact
44:1424:113913:18:18:79:525:439:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:urbanization measures using official census data for the years 1875,  1880,  1885,  1890,  1895,
44:1425:114009:18:19:79:525:421:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:1900,  1905,  1910.   The  corresponding  data  can  be  retrieved  in  the  various  volumes  of  the
44:1426:114111:19:29:79:224:402:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f2:Statistik des deutschen Reichs.

44:1429:114238:19:18:79:306:329:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f2:report with appendices,London; Darling & Son.
