45:1443:115273:0:29:79:514:671:14:g_d0_f1:14:g_d0_f1:Appendix E: Coding Institutional Reform in German Polities
45:1444:115331:29:19:79:525:642:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:In this appendix, we describe in more detail the introduction of reforms in 19th century Ger-
45:1445:115424:19:18:79:525:623:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:many; a list of sources is given below.  A more detailed description of this process in all German
45:1446:115522:18:19:79:360:605:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:pre-unitary states can be found in Acemoglu et. al. (2009).
45:1447:115581:19:18:96:525:586:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:The introduction of the French civil and commercial codes was one of the reforms most
45:1448:115666:18:18:79:525:568:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:systematically pursued in the occupied territories of Germany and the civil code, introduced by
45:1449:115761:18:19:79:525:550:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Napoleon, was in force until 1900 in the territories left of the Rhine.  The codes were enacted
45:1450:115856:19:18:79:525:531:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:in the Rhineland starting in 1805, in Westphalia starting in 1808, in the Grand Duchy of Berg
45:1451:115949:18:19:79:525:513:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:starting in 1810, and starting in 1809/1810 for the territories of northern Germany correspond-
45:1452:116044:19:18:79:525:494:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:ing to present-day Lower Saxony, as well as in the Hanseatic Cities of Bremen, Hamburg, and
45:1453:116135:18:19:79:525:476:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:L ̈ubeck.  At the same time, Baden, under the leadership of its liberal prime minister Johann
45:1454:116228:19:18:79:525:457:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f6:Niklas Friedrich Brauer,  introduced theBadisches  Landrecht,  essentially theCode  Napol ́eon
45:1455:116322:18:18:79:525:439:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:with some minor additions; Bavaria, on the other hand, merely revised some parts of its Codex
45:1456:116415:18:19:79:525:421:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Maximilianeus Bavaricus Civilis of 1756,  which however remained a subsidiary legal source,
45:1457:116506:19:18:79:200:402:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:second to customary law.
45:1458:116530:18:19:96:525:384:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:After the demise of Napoleonic rule in Germany, the territories east of the Rhine were quick
45:1459:116622:19:18:79:525:365:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:in  reintroducing  the  previous  legal  systems  and  dismantling  all  remnants  of  the  Napoleonic
45:1460:116724:18:18:79:525:347:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:reforms.  Two exceptions stand out, though.  The lands that were taken over by Prussia ob-
45:1461:116814:18:19:79:525:329:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:tained theAllgemeines Landrecht(ALR), the ambitious Prussian civil code of 1794, a 19,000
45:1462:116903:19:18:79:525:310:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:paragraphs-long codification of all legal matters which,  while retaining some vestiges of the
45:1463:116997:18:19:79:525:292:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:feudal system, was a progressive work for its times, heavily influenced by the ideals of the En-
45:1464:117093:19:18:79:525:273:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:lightenment.  The other exception is represented by the Rhineland, where the local bourgeoisie
45:1465:117187:18:19:79:525:255:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:successfully defended the presence of theCode Napol ́eon, evidently favorable to their position.
45:1466:117283:19:18:96:525:236:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:The  abolition  of  guilds  is  another  reform  intimately  linked  to  the  abolition  of  the  rem-
45:1467:117385:18:18:79:525:218:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:nants of the ancien r ́egime.  The development mirrors the case of the introduction of the civil
45:1468:117481:18:19:79:525:200:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:code:  guilds are first abolished in the territories on the left bank of the Rhine (1800),  then
45:1469:117577:19:18:79:525:181:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:in the Napoleonic states of Westphalia (1808) and Berg (1809), finally in Northern Germany.
45:1470:117668:18:19:79:525:163:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Restoration of the status quo ante occurred equally quickly in the reactionary states of Han-
45:1471:117761:19:18:79:525:144:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:nover and Hesse-Kassel between 1814 and 1816.  Even the Hanseatic cities reversed the reforms
45:1472:117854:18:19:79:212:126:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:they had been subjected to.
45:1473:117881:19:18:96:525:107:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:The situation in the Prussian territories was varied:  while theGewerbefreiheit(freedom of
45:1474:117971:18:0:79:525:89:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:commerce, including the abolition of guilds) was a pillar of the reforms of Stein and Hardenberg,
46:1475:118070:0:18:79:525:671:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:it extended at first only to the core territories of Prussia at its minimal territorial extension
46:1476:118167:18:19:79:525:653:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:after the Peace of Tilsit. Following the Congress of Vienna, the abolition of guilds was sustained
46:1477:118265:19:18:79:525:634:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:in the Rhineland (both Prussian and non-Prussian) and in the former territories of Berg and
46:1478:118356:18:19:79:135:616:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Westphalia.
46:1479:118367:19:18:96:525:597:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:The policies of no other German state were as consistent with freedom of commerce af-
46:1480:118452:18:19:79:525:579:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:ter 1815 as were those of Prussia;  Baden retained its guild structure, whereas W ̈urttemberg
46:1481:118545:19:18:79:525:560:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:reorganized its guilds in larger units,  allowing for a small degree of mobility within groups.
46:1482:118640:18:18:79:525:542:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Bavaria and Saxony moved instead to a concession-based system, where a state bureaucracy
46:1483:118728:18:19:79:525:524:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:would determine the number of people and the prerequisites to become craftsmen.  A tempo-
46:1484:118817:19:18:79:525:505:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:rary backlash occurred during and after the 1848 revolution,  when there was pressure for a
46:1485:118908:18:19:79:525:487:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:restoration of guild structures in many states that had so far pursued liberal policies, and full
46:1486:119005:19:18:79:525:468:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:liberalization all over Germany was eventually achieved with the newGewerbeordnung(law
46:1487:119091:18:19:79:303:450:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:regulating commerce) after unification in 1871.
46:1488:119138:19:18:96:525:431:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Agrarian reforms are another dimension along which different approaches are discernible
46:1489:119225:18:18:79:525:413:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:across German states, even when restricting one’s view only to the territories west of the Elbe,
46:1490:119321:18:19:79:525:395:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:where the feudal relations were less oppressive than in the eastern territories characterized by
46:1491:119417:19:18:79:525:376:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:serfdom and theGutsherrschaftform of land tenure. Again, we can see that the wave of reforms
46:1492:119509:18:19:79:525:358:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:was lead by the French occupiers first, and by the Prussian ‘defensive modernizers’ thereafter.
46:1493:119604:19:18:79:525:339:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:The  most  radical  attempt  to  reform  succeeded  only  west  of  the  Rhine,  where  serfdom  was
46:1494:119704:18:19:79:525:321:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:abolished without compensation and duties were made redeemable for 15 times their annual
46:1495:119792:19:18:79:145:302:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:value in 1798.
46:1496:119806:18:18:96:525:284:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Reforms followed suit in Berg (1808) and Westphalia (1809), but confusion soon arose about
46:1497:119896:18:19:79:525:266:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the exact terms of the redemption of feudal payments.  All reforms were ultimately blocked
46:1498:119986:19:18:79:525:247:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:by decree in 1812, and resumed only in Prussian times.  In fact, at the same time Prussia was
46:1499:120079:18:19:79:525:229:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:already implementing agrarian reforms in parts of Prussia, starting with the edict of October
46:1500:120172:19:18:79:525:210:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:9th, 1807, which in 1821 was perfected with laws regulating the exact terms of redemption of
46:1501:120264:18:19:79:285:192:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:feudal duties (25 times their annual value).
46:1502:120308:19:18:96:525:173:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f6:A law describing the exact amount needed to exit the feudal relation of theGrundherrschaft
46:1503:120398:18:18:79:525:155:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:was a crucial precondition for agrarian reforms that did not remain a dead letter.  Hence what
46:1504:120492:18:19:79:525:137:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the figures in column 5 of Table 2 report is the introduction of such laws, as well as the abolition
46:1505:120592:19:18:79:394:118:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:of serfdom (a mere formality in most territories west of the Elbe).
46:1506:120659:18:0:96:525:100:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:The  emancipation  of  Jews  is  the  one  reform  that  was  pursued  less  consistently  across
47:1507:120758:0:18:79:525:671:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Germany.  The initial steps taken in the Napoleonic states—the most liberal policy was enacted
47:1508:120852:18:19:79:525:653:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:in  Westphalia—were  rapidly  circumscribed  with  thed ́ecret  infˆameof  1808,  which  limited
47:1509:120948:19:18:79:525:634:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the  occupational  choice  of  Jews  in  the  Rhineland  through  concession-based  system.   In  a
47:1510:121047:18:19:79:525:616:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:similar fashion, Prussia granted wide-ranging freedoms at first through the law of March 1812,
47:1511:121141:19:18:79:525:597:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:but retreated soon afterwards,  when it failed to extend the freedoms to the newly acquired
47:1512:121232:18:19:79:525:579:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:territories.  While full emancipation of the Jews, including political rights, had to wait until
47:1513:121328:19:18:79:525:560:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:unification  in  1871,  some  states  granted  wide-ranging  freedoms  to  their  Jewish  subjects,  in
47:1514:121431:18:18:79:525:542:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:particular with respect to occupational choices.  Baden, Brunswick, Anhalt, and the free city
47:1515:121524:18:30:79:457:524:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:of Frankfurt, where the Rothschild dynasty originated, were examples in point.
